  "content": "# client-go: Advanced Systems Guide\n\n> Repository snapshot: `github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--stripped`\n> Primary tree: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/`\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the canonical Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It serves two distinct audiences: the internal control-plane components (kubelet, kube-controller-manager, scheduler) and external operators and controllers written by third parties. It is not a thin HTTP wrapper; it contains a complete, self-consistent framework for building event-driven controllers that are resilient to API-server restarts, network partitions, and resource-version drift.\n\n### What client-go owns\n\n- **HTTP transport assembly** \u2014 TLS, authentication, rate limiting, retry, and content negotiation.\n- **Typed and untyped client models** \u2014 `kubernetes.Clientset` and `dynamic.DynamicClient`.\n- **Controller infrastructure** \u2014 `Reflector`, `DeltaFIFO`, `Indexer`, `SharedIndexInformer`, `sharedProcessor`, and `workqueue`.\n- **High-level patterns** \u2014 `SharedInformerFactory`, leader election, Server-Side Apply builders, event recording.\n- **Code-generation output** \u2014 typed listers, typed informers, and apply-configuration builders.\n\n### What client-go does NOT own\n\n| Concern | Owner |\n|---------|-------|\n| API object schemas (Pod, Deployment, \u2026) | `k8s.io/api` |\n| Runtime serialization (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR) | `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime` |\n| `kubeconfig` file format | `k8s.io/client-go/tools/clientcmd` (within the library, but logically separate) |\n| API Priority and Fairness server logic | `k8s.io/apiserver` |\n| Code generation tools | `k8s.io/code-generator` |\n\n### Upstream dependencies (what client-go consumes)\n\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery` \u2014 object meta, watch events, list/get options, runtime serializer interfaces.\n- `k8s.io/api` \u2014 concrete API type structs that typed clients encode/decode.\n- `golang.org/x/time/rate` \u2014 token-bucket implementation used by the workqueue rate limiter.\n- `k8s.io/utils/clock` \u2014 injectable clock for testing time-dependent code.\n\n### Downstream dependents (what consumes client-go)\n\n- Every Kubernetes control-plane component (`kube-controller-manager`, `kubelet`, `cloud-controller-manager`).\n- All community and vendor operators, typically via the higher-level `controller-runtime` framework.\n- `kubectl` (via the `dynamic` client and `tools/clientcmd`).\n\n### Versioning contract\n\n`client-go` version `v0.X.Y` aligns with Kubernetes `v1.X.Y`. An older client works against a newer API server (n-3 skew), but not the reverse. This guarantee shapes the entire compatibility surface of the library.\n(`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/ARCHITECTURE.md`, lines 155\u2013162)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Configuration Layer\n\n**`rest.Config`** (`rest/config.go:55`) is the in-memory configuration object. It carries:\n\n- Target host and API path.\n- Authentication credentials: `BearerToken`, `BearerTokenFile` (live-reloaded), `Username`/`Password`, TLS client cert, `ExecProvider` (exec-based credential plugins), `AuthProvider` (legacy plugin interface).\n- Transport customization: `WrapTransport`, `Transport`, `Dial`, `Proxy`.\n- Client-side rate limiting: `QPS` (default 5.0), `Burst` (default 10).\n- Content negotiation: `ContentType`, `AcceptContentTypes`.\n\nTwo canonical factories produce a `Config`:\n\n- `InClusterConfig()` (`rest/config.go:543`) \u2014 reads the pod service-account token from `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token` and CA from `/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt`.\n- `tools/clientcmd` \u2014 merges `kubeconfig` files, resolves contexts, and handles exec-based auth.\n\n`Config.String()` and `Config.GoString()` redact sensitive fields (`BearerToken`, `Password`, `KeyData`) so that the struct can safely be logged (`rest/config.go:192`).\n\n### 2.2 Transport Layer\n\n`HTTPClientFor(config)` \u2192 `TransportFor(config)` \u2192 `transport.New(cfg)` (`rest/transport.go:32`).\n\n`transport.HTTPWrappersForConfig` (`transport/round_trippers.go:41`) assembles a chain of `http.RoundTripper` decorators in a fixed order:\n\n1. **Custom `WrapTransport`** \u2014 caller-injected.\n2. **`DebugWrappers`** \u2014 activated when `klog` verbosity \u2265 6; emits per-request HTTP traces.\n3. **Auth wrapper** \u2014 exactly one of: `BearerAuthWithRefreshRoundTripper` (reads the token file on each request), `BasicAuthRoundTripper`, or nothing.\n4. **`UserAgentRoundTripper`** \u2014 appends `User-Agent: <binary>/<version> (<os>/<arch>) kubernetes/<commit>`.\n5. **`ImpersonatingRoundTripper`** \u2014 injects `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` headers.\n\nThe outer `http.Client` has a configurable `Timeout` and shares a connection pool per `Config.Host`. Because the auth wrapper reads `BearerTokenFile` on every call, credential rotation happens transparently without restarting the client.\n\n### 2.3 REST Client\n\n**`RESTClient`** (`rest/client.go:86`) is the foundational HTTP client. It exposes a builder-pattern request API (`Verb()`, `Resource()`, `Namespace()`, `Name()`, `Body()`, `Do()`, `Watch()`, `Stream()`).\n\nThe **`Request`** struct (`rest/request.go:96`) accumulates path segments, query parameters, headers, and a body, then dispatches the assembled HTTP request through the shared `http.Client`. Key behaviors:\n\n- **Rate limiting** \u2014 each `Request` holds a reference to the shared `flowcontrol.RateLimiter`. `Request.Do()` calls `rateLimiter.Wait()` before sending, throttling bursts against the configured QPS. Throttle events exceeding `longThrottleLatency` (50ms) are logged at v4; those exceeding `extraLongThrottleLatency` (1s) at v2 (`rest/request.go:54`).\n- **Retry on 429/5xx** \u2014 the `WithRetry` interface (`rest/with_retry.go:53`) controls retry behavior. The default `withRetry` implementation reads the `Retry-After` header from `429 Too Many Requests` responses and backs off accordingly. This is the client-side complement to API Priority and Fairness.\n- **Content negotiation** \u2014 the `Accept` header is set from `AcceptContentTypes` or `ContentType`. Controllers that only need metadata can request `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` to reduce payload size.\n- **Watch** \u2014 `Request.Watch()` returns a `watch.Interface` backed by a chunked HTTP response decoder (`rest/watch/`). Each decoded chunk is emitted as a `watch.Event` with type `ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, or `BOOKMARK`.\n\n### 2.4 Typed Clientset\n\n**`kubernetes.Clientset`** (`kubernetes/`) is a code-generated struct that composes one typed client per API group version. Every typed client is a thin adapter that calls `RESTClientFor` with a fixed `GroupVersion` and delegates to the `Request` builder. This provides compile-time type safety: errors from wrong resource kinds surface at build time, not runtime.\n\n### 2.5 Dynamic Client\n\n**`dynamic.DynamicClient`** (`dynamic/simple.go:34`) wraps a `rest.Interface` and works with `unstructured.Unstructured` maps. It is schema-agnostic and can interact with any API group, including CRDs, without generated code. The tradeoff is that all field access is string-keyed, losing compile-time safety.\n\n`ConfigFor` (`dynamic/simple.go:42`) forcibly sets `ContentType` to `application/json` (or optionally `application/cbor` when the `ClientsPreferCBOR` feature gate is enabled), because the dynamic client has no registered serializer for protobuf.\n\n### 2.6 Controller Infrastructure (`tools/cache`)\n\nThis package contains the building blocks of every event-driven controller in Kubernetes.\n\n#### `ListerWatcher` and `ListWatch`\n\n`ListWatch` (`tools/cache/listwatch.go:193`) implements `ListerWatcherWithContext` by composing a list function and a watch function. `NewFilteredListWatchFromClient` (`tools/cache/listwatch.go:229`) constructs both from a `Getter` (the REST client) with an optional field/label selector modifier. The list function uses `pager.New` internally through the `Reflector`, so direct callers of `ListWatch.List()` receive unpaginated results.\n\n#### `Reflector`\n\n**`Reflector`** (`tools/cache/reflector.go:87`) is the bridge between the Kubernetes API server and the in-process store. Its single exported behavior is expressed through `RunWithContext`, which calls `ListAndWatchWithContext` in a loop, managed by an exponential backoff manager (`800ms` base, `30s` cap, resetting after `2min` of stability).\n\n`ListAndWatchWithContext` (`tools/cache/reflector.go:408`) does one of two things depending on the `WatchListClient` feature gate:\n\n- **Classic mode** (`fallbackToList = true`): calls `r.list()`, which uses `pager.ListWithAlloc` to retrieve all objects in chunks. The returned `resourceVersion` is stored and used to open a `WATCH` from that exact point.\n- **WatchList mode** (`useWatchList = true`): opens a single streaming watch with `ResourceVersionMatch=NotOlderThan`, receiving synthetic `ADDED` events followed by a terminal `BOOKMARK` that signals sync completion. This consumes significantly fewer server resources than paginated LIST.\n\nThe `watch` inner loop (`tools/cache/reflector.go:499`) runs until the context is canceled or a non-retriable error occurs. For each received `watch.Event` it calls `handleWatch`, which routes the event into the `ReflectorStore`. `BOOKMARK` events update `lastSyncResourceVersion` without touching the store.\n\nWatch timeout randomization (`minWatchTimeout` to `2\u00d7minWatchTimeout`, default 5-10 minutes) spreads reconnection load across the API server's watch cache.\n\n#### `DeltaFIFO`\n\n**`DeltaFIFO`** (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go:63`) is the producer-consumer queue between the Reflector and the rest of the informer machinery. Its key design property: it accumulates *all* deltas for a given object key, not just the latest state. When the consumer calls `Pop()`, it receives the full slice of deltas that arrived since the last pop. This means a controller that processes slowly will see every intermediate state batched together rather than losing events.\n\nDelta types: `Added`, `Updated`, `Deleted`, `Replaced` (from LIST/Replace calls), `Sync` (from periodic resync). `KnownObjects` links the FIFO to the downstream `Indexer` so that `Replace()` can synthesize `Deleted` deltas for objects missing from the new list.\n\n#### `Indexer` and `ThreadSafeStore`\n\n**`Indexer`** (`tools/cache/index.go:35`) extends `Store` with secondary index support. The concrete implementation (`threadSafeMap` inside `tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`) holds a map from key to object and a map of named indices. Each index is an `IndexFunc` (`tools/cache/index.go:58`) that returns a set of string-valued index keys for a given object. The built-in `MetaNamespaceIndexFunc` indexes by namespace.\n\n`ByIndex(indexName, indexedValue)` performs a reverse lookup: given an index name and a specific value (e.g., a namespace string), it returns all matching objects. This is the mechanism that makes operations like \"list all pods in namespace X\" O(1) against the local cache instead of requiring a full scan.\n\n#### `SharedIndexInformer` and `sharedProcessor`\n\n**`sharedIndexInformer`** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:415`) combines an `Indexer`, an internal `Controller` (which runs the `Reflector` and pops the `DeltaFIFO`), and a `sharedProcessor`. It is the main informer type used in production.\n\n`RunWithContext` (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:529`) does:\n1. Constructs a `DeltaFIFO` keyed to the `Indexer`.\n2. Builds a `Config` with `HandleDeltas` as the `ProcessFunc`.\n3. Creates and runs the internal `Controller`.\n4. Concurrently runs the `sharedProcessor` and `CacheMutationDetector`.\n\n`HandleDeltas` is the critical function that holds the `DeltaFIFO` lock while it:\n1. Updates the `Indexer` for each delta.\n2. Enqueues the corresponding notification (add/update/delete) into the `sharedProcessor`.\n\nThe **`sharedProcessor`** fans out notifications to all registered `processorListener`s. Each listener has a ring buffer (`utils/buffer`) that decouples notification production from handler execution. This means a slow handler does not block the watch loop, but will accumulate notifications in its buffer. If the buffer fills, the listener blocks, which eventually blocks the `DeltaFIFO` pop loop.\n\n**`SharedInformerFactory`** (`informers/factory.go:57`) is the standard entry point for production controllers. It acts as a registry of `SharedIndexInformer` instances keyed by `reflect.Type`, ensuring that a single informer (and therefore a single LIST/WATCH connection) is shared across multiple controllers watching the same resource type.\n\n### 2.7 Workqueue\n\n**`util/workqueue`** provides three layers:\n\n- `TypedInterface[T]` (`util/workqueue/queue.go:30`) \u2014 a basic FIFO with deduplication: adding an already-queued key is a no-op, and adding a key that is currently being processed queues it for re-processing after `Done()` is called.\n- `TypedDelayingInterface[T]` \u2014 adds `AddAfter(item, delay)` for scheduled re-queuing (used for exponential backoff).\n- `TypedRateLimitingInterface[T]` \u2014 wraps the delaying queue with a `TypedRateLimiter`.\n\n**`DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter`** (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go:50`) composes two limiters with `MaxOf`:\n- `TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter` \u2014 per-item exponential backoff starting at 5ms, capped at 1000s. This is the per-item retry backoff seen in controller reconcile loops.\n- `TypedBucketRateLimiter` \u2014 global token bucket at 10 QPS with burst 100. This prevents a flood of fast-failing items from hammering the API server.\n\n### 2.8 Leader Election\n\n**`tools/leaderelection`** provides distributed leader election via a Kubernetes `Lease` resource (or `ConfigMap`/`Endpoints` for backward compatibility). The `LeaderElector.Run` lifecycle:\n\n1. **Acquire** \u2014 calls `tryAcquireOrRenew` in a jittered loop at `RetryPeriod` intervals until the `Lease` is acquired or the context is canceled.\n2. **Lead** \u2014 launches `OnStartedLeading(ctx)` in a goroutine, then calls `renew` in a tight loop.\n3. **Renew** \u2014 calls `tryAcquireOrRenew` every `RetryPeriod` within a `RenewDeadline` window. Failure to renew within the deadline cancels the leading context, triggering cleanup.\n4. **Stop** \u2014 always calls `OnStoppedLeading()`.\n\nThe implementation explicitly does not guarantee a single writer (no fencing tokens), relying instead on API server optimistic concurrency (`resourceVersion` conflict detection) and bounded lease duration to limit dual-leader windows. The `LeaseDuration`:`RenewDeadline` ratio controls tolerance to clock skew.\n\n### 2.9 Server-Side Apply Builders\n\n**`applyconfigurations/`** contains generated structs that represent partial, nullable views of API objects for use with `PATCH application/apply-patch+yaml`. Unlike full object structs, apply-configuration structs omit unset fields entirely rather than serializing zero values, preventing accidental ownership of fields the controller doesn't manage. These are constructed with a fluent builder API and passed to a typed client's `Apply()` method.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Simple CRUD Request\n\n```\nUser code\n  \u2192 kubernetes.Clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"ns\")\n      \u2192 typed client calls RESTClient.Get().Namespace(\"ns\").Resource(\"pods\").Name(\"my-pod\")\n          \u2192 Request.Do(ctx)\n              \u2192 rateLimiter.Wait(ctx)           [client-side token bucket]\n              \u2192 http.Client.Do(assembledReq)    [transport chain: debug \u2192 auth \u2192 impersonate]\n              \u2192 response body decoded via NegotiatedSerializer\n              \u2192 on non-2xx: deserialize into errors.StatusError\n              \u2192 on 429/5xx: withRetry.IsNextRetry() \u2192 backoff \u2192 retry\n```\n\nThe `GroupVersion` embedded in each typed client's `RESTClient` sets the `Accept` header automatically to the correct API version. The client never needs to know the resource's URL structure beyond `Resource()`, `Namespace()`, and `Name()`.\n\n### 3.2 Informer Startup and Watch Loop\n\n```\nSharedInformerFactory.Start(stopCh)\n  \u2192 for each registered SharedIndexInformer, goroutine: informer.RunWithContext(ctx)\n\nsharedIndexInformer.RunWithContext(ctx)\n  \u251c\u2500 goroutine: sharedProcessor.run(processorCtx)       [fan-out to handlers]\n  \u251c\u2500 goroutine: cacheMutationDetector.Run(processorCtx) [debug mode only]\n  \u2514\u2500 controller.RunWithContext(ctx)\n       \u251c\u2500 goroutine: Reflector.RunWithContext(ctx)\n       \u2502    \u2514\u2500 loop: ListAndWatchWithContext(ctx)\n       \u2502         \u251c\u2500 list(): pager.ListWithAlloc \u2192 DeltaFIFO.Replace()\n       \u2502         \u2502       [populates Indexer; emits Replaced/Sync deltas]\n       \u2502         \u2514\u2500 watch(): listerWatcher.WatchWithContext \u2192 handleWatch\n       \u2502              [per event: DeltaFIFO.Add/Update/Delete]\n       \u2514\u2500 loop: DeltaFIFO.Pop(HandleDeltas)\n            HandleDeltas(deltas):\n              \u251c\u2500 Indexer.Add/Update/Delete          [updates in-process cache]\n              \u2514\u2500 sharedProcessor.distribute(notif)  [enqueues to each listener's buffer]\n\nprocessorListener.run() goroutine (one per handler):\n  \u2514\u2500 loop: dequeue from ring buffer \u2192 handler.OnAdd / OnUpdate / OnDelete\n\nUser controller event handler (example):\n  \u2514\u2500 OnAdd(obj) { workqueue.Add(keyOf(obj)) }\n\nController reconcile goroutine (user code):\n  \u2514\u2500 loop: workqueue.Get() \u2192 reconcile(key) \u2192 workqueue.Done(key)\n       reconcile(key):\n         \u251c\u2500 lister.Pods(\"ns\").Get(name)   [reads Indexer, no API call]\n         \u2514\u2500 typed client.Pods(\"ns\").Update(...)  [API call only on mutation]\n```\n\nThe critical design insight: the `workqueue` decouples event arrival from reconciliation. Events arrive at watch speed; reconciliation happens at the controller's pace with built-in deduplication and retry backoff.\n\n### 3.3 Resync\n\nResync does not contact the API server. The `Reflector.startResync` goroutine fires the `ShouldResync` callback periodically. When it returns true, `DeltaFIFO.Resync()` iterates the `Indexer`'s keys and enqueues a `Sync` delta for each. This causes `HandleDeltas` to re-invoke the event handler's `OnUpdate` with the current cached object, giving the controller a chance to reconcile state it may have missed.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 `resourceVersion` Staleness\n\nThe Reflector tracks `lastSyncResourceVersion`. If the API server's watch cache does not retain history back to that version (defaulting to 5 minutes of history), the watch returns a `410 Gone` error. The Reflector handles this by calling `setIsLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable(true)` and re-listing with `ResourceVersion=\"\"` (latest) rather than the stale version, accepting a momentary full scan of etcd or the watch cache (`tools/cache/reflector.go:633`).\n\n**Operational implication**: during control-plane upgrades or API server restarts, every informer will relist. At large scale, concurrent relisters from many controllers can create a \"thundering herd\" against etcd. The watch cache mitigates this, but clusters with the watch cache disabled face significant load spikes.\n\n### 4.2 Slow Event Handlers and Back-pressure\n\nThe `sharedProcessor`'s per-listener ring buffer (`utils/buffer`) is pre-allocated at `initialBufferSize = 1024` events (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:340`). When a handler is slow, the buffer fills. Once full, `sharedProcessor.distribute()` blocks, which blocks `HandleDeltas`, which blocks `DeltaFIFO.Pop()`, which eventually stalls the `Reflector`'s event consumption. A stalled watch connection can be closed by the API server's idle timeout.\n\nThe comment in the `SharedInformer` interface documentation is explicit:\n> \"A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of notifications.\" (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:130`)\n\nThis is why all production controllers hand off work to a `workqueue` in the handler rather than processing inline.\n\n### 4.3 Client-Side Rate Limiting vs. API Priority and Fairness\n\nThe `QPS`/`Burst` token bucket in `RESTClient` is a client-side rate limiter. It protects the API server by smoothing request bursts from a single client. Kubernetes API server's API Priority and Fairness (APF) provides server-side flow control that also covers rate abuse from misconfigured clients. These two systems are complementary: the client-side limiter prevents reaching the server-side queue; APF handles cases where the client ignores its own limits or where aggregate load exceeds cluster capacity.\n\nSetting `QPS` to -1 disables client-side limiting entirely. This is appropriate only for special clients like the controller manager's leader-election paths that must not be queued, but is dangerous in general.\n\n### 4.4 Leader Election Gaps\n\nThe `LeaderElector` does not guarantee a single leader at any instant. If the leader process is paused (GC stop-the-world, CPU starvation, OS scheduling jitter), it may fail to renew the lease within `RenewDeadline`, causing another candidate to acquire the lease before the original leader has stopped acting. The `LeaseDuration` should be set long enough to absorb expected scheduling jitter while the `RenewDeadline`/`RetryPeriod` ratio determines recovery speed. The comment in the package documentation notes:\n> \"This implementation does not guarantee that only one client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\" (`tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go:20`)\n\nFor operations that require strict single-writer semantics (e.g., writing to external systems), callers must implement their own idempotency or fencing on top of the leader election lease.\n\n### 4.5 SharedInformerFactory and Goroutine Proliferation\n\nEach `SharedIndexInformer` started by `SharedInformerFactory.Start()` spawns at minimum two goroutines: the Reflector loop and the `sharedProcessor`. Each registered event handler adds another goroutine (the `processorListener.run` loop). In controllers watching many resource types with many handlers, the total goroutine count grows proportionally. This is by design but must be considered during resource planning.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Custom `http.RoundTripper` via `WrapTransport`\n\n`rest.Config.WrapTransport` (`rest/config.go:115`) is called after the base transport is assembled. It is the primary extension point for cross-cutting HTTP concerns: distributed tracing (injecting `traceparent` headers), custom metrics, or mutual TLS certificate rotation. The convention is to wrap rather than replace, preserving the auth and debug layers already in place.\n\n**Risk**: A `WrapTransport` that blocks or returns errors drops all requests from the affected client. Panics inside the wrapper will propagate and crash the using goroutine.\n\n### 5.2 `ExecProvider` for External Credential Plugins\n\n`rest.Config.ExecProvider` (`rest/config.go:92`) delegates credential retrieval to an external binary (e.g., `aws eks get-token`). The `exec` package (`plugin/pkg/client/auth/exec/`) caches credentials and re-executes the binary when they expire. This is the standard mechanism for cloud-provider authentication without embedding credentials.\n\n**Risk**: If the exec binary is slow or unavailable, all API calls block waiting for credentials. The exec plugin runs in a goroutine per client, so deadlines on the parent context propagate, but errors surface as generic transport errors rather than auth-specific ones.\n\n### 5.3 `TransformFunc` on Informers\n\n`SharedInformer.SetTransform(handler TransformFunc)` (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:231`) installs a function called on each object before it is inserted into the `Indexer`. Common uses:\n\n- Stripping `managedFields` to reduce memory usage.\n- Normalizing fields before indexing.\n- Scrubbing sensitive data from the in-memory cache.\n\nThe transform runs synchronously in the `DeltaFIFO.Pop` path, under the FIFO lock. It must not access the informer's `Indexer` (deadlock risk) or perform slow I/O (back-pressure on the watch loop). Must be set before calling `Run()`.\n\n### 5.4 Custom `Indexers`\n\nAdditional `IndexFunc` entries can be registered on a `SharedIndexInformer` via `AddIndexers()` before the informer starts (`tools/cache/index.go:58`). Custom indexes enable efficient lookups beyond namespace, such as indexing pods by node name or services by `spec.selector` labels. Each index function must be deterministic and cheap, since it runs on every object mutation.\n\n**Risk**: Adding indexes after the informer starts returns an error. Index functions that panic will crash the goroutine processing that delta.\n\n### 5.5 `WatchErrorHandler`\n\n`SharedInformer.SetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext()` installs a callback invoked whenever `ListAndWatch` drops its connection. The default handler logs at different levels based on error type (`io.EOF` is silent, `io.ErrUnexpectedEOF` is logged at v1, others trigger `HandleError`). A custom handler can emit metrics or alerts. The handler runs in the Reflector's goroutine context and must return quickly.\n\n### 5.6 Custom `WorkQueue` Backend\n\n`TypedQueueConfig.Queue` (`util/workqueue/queue.go:98`) accepts an alternative queue implementation. The default is a slice-based FIFO. Custom implementations can support priority queuing (for example, preferring recently-changed objects) by implementing `Queue[T].Touch()`, which is called when a key that is already in the queue is added again.\n\n### 5.7 `ResourceLock` Interface for Leader Election\n\n`tools/leaderelection/resourcelock.Interface` defines the lock abstraction used by `LeaderElector`. The standard implementations use `Lease`, `ConfigMap`, or `Endpoints` Kubernetes objects. Custom implementations could use external systems (e.g., etcd directly or a database), provided they implement optimistic concurrency semantics.\n\n### 5.8 Server-Side Apply and Generated `applyconfigurations`\n\nFor controllers that co-manage objects with other controllers or users, Server-Side Apply via the `applyconfigurations/` builders is strongly preferred over `get-modify-update`. The controller sets only the fields it owns; the server merges with fields owned by other managers. Custom field managers can be named per-controller.\n\n**Risk**: Using full object `Update()` in a controller that coexists with Server-Side Apply will conflict with `managedFields` ownership. Mixing paradigms on the same object causes repeated update conflicts.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance\n\n**Memory**: Each `SharedIndexInformer` holds a full in-memory copy of all objects of its type. A cluster with 100,000 pods, each 10 KB serialized, will use ~1 GB of cache per informer instance watching pods. `SetTransform` stripping `managedFields` and `status.conditions` can reduce this significantly (often 50-70% for pod objects).\n\n**CPU**: `sharedProcessor` uses a ring buffer that avoids allocations per notification. `DeltaFIFO` uses a `sync.Cond` for producer/consumer coordination, avoiding busy-polling. The main CPU cost at steady state is JSON/protobuf decoding of watch events plus index maintenance.\n\n**Network**: Each `SharedIndexInformer` opens one persistent HTTP/2 stream (watch connection). With HTTP/2 multiplexing, a single TCP connection can serve multiple watches. Protobuf (`application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf`) is ~30-40% more compact than JSON and is the default for typed clients; this reduces bandwidth especially for large objects.\n\n**Rate limiting**: The default `QPS=5, Burst=10` in `rest.Config` is appropriate for controllers doing occasional reconciliation. Controllers that list or update many objects per reconcile loop (e.g., managing 1,000 Pods per second) must raise these values, balancing against APF priority levels on the server.\n\n### Reliability\n\n**Watch reconnect**: The Reflector's exponential backoff (base 800ms, cap 30s, jitter) prevents stampede after an API server restart. After 2 minutes of stable operation the backoff resets, ensuring normal watch reconnection latency returns to near-zero.\n\n**`HasSynced()`**: Controllers should gate reconciliation on `WaitForNamedCacheSync` or `WaitForNamedCacheSyncWithContext`. `HasSynced()` returns `true` only after the informer has completed its initial LIST. Acting before sync may cause controllers to re-create objects that already exist, generating unnecessary updates and potential conflicts.\n\n**Handler panic recovery**: `sharedIndexInformer.RunWithContext` wraps with `utilruntime.HandleCrashWithContext`, which logs panics and continues running. However, panics inside user-supplied event handlers running in `processorListener.run` goroutines are not caught by this wrapper \u2014 they must be caught by the user, or the listener goroutine terminates silently and the handler stops receiving events.\n\n### Maintainability\n\n**Code generation**: The typed clients, listers, and informers in `kubernetes/`, `listers/`, and `informers/` are fully generated by `hack/update-codegen.sh`. Manual edits will be overwritten. Any modification to a built-in API type requires regenerating all three layers. Custom resource types follow the same pattern using `k8s.io/code-generator`.\n\n**Feature gates**: Several behaviors are controlled by `k8s.io/client-go/features` gate checks at runtime. Notable gates: `WatchListClient` (streaming initialization), `ClientsAllowCBOR` / `ClientsPreferCBOR` (CBOR wire format), `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` (batch delta processing). Enabling these in production without testing in staging first can change memory and CPU behavior non-trivially.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Critical File Map\n\n| Path | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/ARCHITECTURE.md` | Authoritative architectural overview from maintainers |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/config.go` | `rest.Config` struct; `InClusterConfig()`; `RESTClientFor()`; rate limiter initialization |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/client.go` | `RESTClient` struct; `NewRESTClient()`; `Interface` definition |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/request.go` | `Request` builder; rate limit enforcement; retry loop; `Do()`, `Watch()`, `Stream()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/with_retry.go` | `WithRetry` interface; 429/5xx backoff contract |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/transport.go` | `HTTPClientFor()`; `TransportFor()`; delegates to `transport.New()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/transport/round_trippers.go` | `HTTPWrappersForConfig()`; assembles auth/debug/user-agent/impersonation chain |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/dynamic/simple.go` | `DynamicClient`; `ConfigFor()` forcing JSON content type |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go` | `ListerWatcher`, `ListerWatcherWithContext` interfaces; `ListWatch`; `NewFilteredListWatchFromClient()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go` | `Reflector`; `ListAndWatchWithContext()`; `list()`; `watchList()`; `watch()` loop; backoff manager |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` | `DeltaFIFO`; delta accumulation semantics; `Replace()` logic for resync |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/store.go` | `Store` interface; `TransactionStore`; `KeyFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go` | `Indexer` interface; `IndexFunc`; `MetaNamespaceIndexFunc` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go` | Low-level `Controller` and `Config`; `ProcessFunc`; bridges Reflector to `DeltaFIFO.Pop` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go` | `SharedInformer`/`SharedIndexInformer` interfaces; `sharedIndexInformer`; `sharedProcessor`; `HandleDeltas`; `WaitForCacheSync` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/factory.go` | `SharedInformerFactory`; per-type informer registry; `WithTransform`/`WithTweakListOptions` options |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go` | `TypedInterface`; deduplication semantics; `TypedQueueConfig` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` | `DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter()`; per-item exponential + global token bucket |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go` | `AddAfter()` for scheduled re-queuing |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go` | `LeaderElector`; `LeaderElectionConfig`; `acquire()`/`renew()` lifecycle |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/` | `Interface` for the lock backend; `Lease`, `ConfigMap`, `Endpoints` implementations |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Generated Server-Side Apply builder structs per API type |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/features/` | Feature gate definitions (`WatchListClient`, `ClientsAllowCBOR`, etc.) |\n",

# client-go: Advanced Systems Guide

> Repository snapshot: `github.com/sg-benchmarks/kubernetes--stripped`
> Primary tree: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/`

---

## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies

`client-go` is the canonical Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It serves two distinct audiences: the internal control-plane components (kubelet, kube-controller-manager, scheduler) and external operators and controllers written by third parties. It is not a thin HTTP wrapper; it contains a complete, self-consistent framework for building event-driven controllers that are resilient to API-server restarts, network partitions, and resource-version drift.

### What client-go owns

- **HTTP transport assembly** — TLS, authentication, rate limiting, retry, and content negotiation.
- **Typed and untyped client models** — `kubernetes.Clientset` and `dynamic.DynamicClient`.
- **Controller infrastructure** — `Reflector`, `DeltaFIFO`, `Indexer`, `SharedIndexInformer`, `sharedProcessor`, and `workqueue`.
- **High-level patterns** — `SharedInformerFactory`, leader election, Server-Side Apply builders, event recording.
- **Code-generation output** — typed listers, typed informers, and apply-configuration builders.

### What client-go does NOT own

| Concern | Owner |
|---------|-------|
| API object schemas (Pod, Deployment, …) | `k8s.io/api` |
| Runtime serialization (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR) | `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime` |
| `kubeconfig` file format | `k8s.io/client-go/tools/clientcmd` (within the library, but logically separate) |
| API Priority and Fairness server logic | `k8s.io/apiserver` |
| Code generation tools | `k8s.io/code-generator` |

### Upstream dependencies (what client-go consumes)

- `k8s.io/apimachinery` — object meta, watch events, list/ge
... (truncated)
